In 2002, Bhutto and the MQM made a side-line deal with Musharraf that allows both to continue underground political activities in Sindh and Kashmir, and to fill the gap after Musharraf had destroyed Sharif's presence in the both provinces. The effects of the arrests was seen clearly in the <a href="/wiki/Pakistani_general_election,_2008" title="Pakistani general election, 2008">2008 parliamentary elections</a>, when Nawaz Sharif failed to secure support back in those two provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-Lieven449_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lieven449-225">[224]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charges_of_corruption">Charges of corruption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benazir_Bhutto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Charges of corruption">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Corruption_charges_against_Benazir_Bhutto_and_Asif_Ali_Zardari" title="Corruption charges against Benazir Bhutto and Asif Ali Zardari">Corruption charges against Benazir Bhutto and Asif Ali Zardari</a></div>
<p>After President Ghulam Ishaq Khan dismissed Bhutto's first government on 6 August 1990 because of corruption allegations, the government of Pakistan directed its intelligence agencies to investigate. Nawaz Sharif became prime minister in the ensuing elections and intensified prosecution investigation of Bhutto. Pakistani embassies through western Europe—in France, Switzerland, Spain, Poland and Britain—were directed to investigate. Bhutto and her husband Zardari faced several legal proceedings, including a charge in Switzerland of money-landering through <a href="/wiki/Banking_in_Switzerland" title="Banking in Switzerland">Swiss banks</a>. While never convicted, Zardari spent eight years in prison on similar corruption charges. Released on bail in 2004, Zardari hinted that while in prison he was tortured; human rights groups have supported his claim that his rights were violated.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[225]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 1998 <i>New York Times</i> (NYT) investigative report<sup id="cite_ref-jld1_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jld1-227">[226]</a></sup> claims that Pakistani investigators have documents that outine a network of bank accounts, all linked to the family's lawyer in Switzerland<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (May 2016)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup>, naming <a href="/wiki/Asif_Zardari" class="mw-redirect" title="Asif Zardari">Asif Zardari</a> as the principal shareholder. According to the NYT article, documents released by the French authorities indicate that Zardari offered exclusive rights to <a href="/wiki/Dassault" class="mw-redirect" title="Dassault">Dassault</a>, a French aircraft manufacturer, to replace the aging <a href="/wiki/Fighter_aircraft" title="Fighter aircraft">fighter jets</a> of the Indian Air Force in exchange for a 5% commission to be paid to a Swiss corporation he controlled. The article also said that a Dubai company received an exclusive license to import gold into Pakistan, for which it paid more than $10 million into Zardari's Dubai-based <a href="/wiki/Citibank" title="Citibank">Citibank</a> accounts. The owner of the Dubai company denied making the payments and said the documents were forged.</p>
<p>Bhutto maintained that the charges against her and her husband were purely political.<sup id="cite_ref-Husband_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Husband-228">[227]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[228]</a></sup> A report by a Pakistani <a href="/wiki/Auditor_General_of_Pakistan" title="Auditor General of Pakistan">auditor-general</a> (AGP) supports Bhutto's claim. It presents information suggesting that Benazir Bhutto was ousted from power in 1990 as the result of a witch hunt approved by then-president <a href="/wiki/Ghulam_Ishaq_Khan" title="Ghulam Ishaq Khan">Ghulam Ishaq Khan</a>. The AGP report says Khan illegally paid legal advisers 28 million rupees to file 19 corruption cases against Bhutto and her husband in 1990–92.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[229]</a></sup></p>
<p>Yet the assets held by Bhutto and her husband continue to be scrutinised and to generate speculation. Prosecutors have alleged that the couple's Swiss bank accounts contain £740 million.<sup id="cite_ref-jld2_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jld2-231">[230]</a></sup> Zardari also bought a neo-<a href="/wiki/Tudor_style_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Tudor style architecture">Tudor</a> mansion and estate worth over £4 million in <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a>, England.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[231]</a></sup> Pakistani investigations have tied other overseas properties to Zardari's family. These include a $2.5 million manor in <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a> owned by Zardari's parents, who had only modest assets at the time of his marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-jld1_227-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jld1-227">[226]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Panama_Papers">Panama Papers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benazir_Bhutto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Panama Papers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bhutto was a client of <a href="/wiki/Mossack_Fonseca" title="Mossack Fonseca">Mossack Fonseca</a>, whose customer records were disclosed in the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Papers" title="Panama Papers">Panama Papers</a> leak. 7 September 2001 London law firm Richard Rooney and Co told MF-BVI (mossack fonseca British virgin island) to create Petroline International Inc in the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[232]</a></sup> Petroline International Inc is owned by Bhutto, her nephew Hassan Ali Jaffery Bhutto, and her aide and head of security <a href="/wiki/Rehman_Malik" title="Rehman Malik">Rehman Malik</a>, who later became a Senator and Interior Minister in the government of <a href="/wiki/Yousaf_Raza_Gillani" title="Yousaf Raza Gillani">Yousaf Raza Gillani</a>. Mossack Fonseca had declined to do business with Bhutto's first company, similarly-named Petrofine FZC, established in <a href="/wiki/Sharjah" title="Sharjah">Sharjah</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> (UAE). in 2000. Petrofine was "politically sensitive" they said, and "declined to accept Mrs Bhutto as a client."<sup id="cite_ref-MFBhutto_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFBhutto-234">[233]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> committee chaired by former head of the US <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Reserve">Federal Reserve</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Volcker" title="Paul Volcker">Paul Volcker</a>, concluded in a 2005 investigation into abuses of the <a href="/wiki/Oil-for-Food_Programme" title="Oil-for-Food Programme">oil-for-food</a> program that Petrofine FZC had paid US$2 million to the <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> government of <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a> to obtain US $115–145 million in oil contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-Off_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Off-235">[234]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, the Pakistani <a href="/wiki/National_Accountability_Bureau" title="National Accountability Bureau">National Accountability Bureau</a> (NAB) accused Bhutto, Malik and Ali Jaffery of owning Petrofine. Bhutto and the PPP denied this. In April 2006 an NAB court froze assets owned in Pakistan and elsewhere by Bhutto and Zardari. The $1.5 billion in assets were acquired through corrupt practices, the NAB said, and noting that the 1997 Swiss charges of criminal money-laundering were still in litigation.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[235]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the request of Pakistan, <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">Interpol</a> issued a request in 2006 for the arrest of Bhutto and her husband on corruption charges. The Bhuttos questioned the legality of the requests in a letter to Interpol.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[236]</a></sup> On 27 January 2007, she was invited by the United States to speak to President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> and Congressional and State Department officials.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[237]</a></sup></p>
<p>In mid-2002 Musharraf implemented a two-term limit on prime ministers. Both Bhutto and Musharraf's other chief rival, Nawaz Sharif, had already served two terms as prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[238]</a></sup> She was in Dubai while the PPP contested the October 2002 general election; it received the largest number of votes but only 63 seats in the National Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008110_220-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008110-220">[219]</a></sup> Musharraf agreed to release Zardari in November 2004 as a symbol of good will; following his release, Zardari travelled to Dubai to be with his wife.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008110Mu.C3.B1oz2013118_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008110Mu.C3.B1oz2013118-240">[239]</a></sup></p>
<p>Figures in the PPP alleged that Musharraf held a longstanding animosity towards Bhutto and her family because under her father, Musharraf's father has been sacked from his position, accused of involvement in a scam.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008113_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008113-241">[240]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_life">Later life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benazir_Bhutto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Later life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Negotiating_a_return_to_Pakistan:_2006–07"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Negotiating_a_return_to_Pakistan:_2006.E2.80.9307">Negotiating a return to Pakistan: 2006–07</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benazir_Bhutto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Negotiating a return to Pakistan: 2006–07">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The US and UK were losing faith with Musharraf.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013114_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013114-242">[241]</a></sup> His domestic popularity was slipping; a mid-2007 poll gave him only a 26% approval rating.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008115_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008115-243">[242]</a></sup> In 2007, mass anti-Musharraf protests broke out in what was known as the <a href="/wiki/Lawyers%27_Movement" title="Lawyers' Movement">Lawyers' Movement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013114_242-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013114-242">[241]</a></sup> Pakistan was also experiencing growing levels of violence from Islamist militants, such as the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Lal_Masjid" title="Siege of Lal Masjid">Siege of Lal Masjid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013114_242-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013114-242">[241]</a></sup> Official figures held that 8 <a href="/wiki/Suicide_bombing" class="mw-redirect" title="Suicide bombing">suicide bombings</a> took place in 2006 and 44 in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013114_242-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013114-242">[241]</a></sup> The US government increasingly saw Bhutto as an important figure who could help to constrain Pakistan's domestic problems.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013113_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013113-244">[243]</a></sup> They nevertheless wanted a power sharing deal and did not want Musharraf removed from power completely, regarding him as a vital ally in their <a href="/wiki/War_on_Terror" title="War on Terror">War on Terror</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013119_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013119-245">[244]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benazir_BhuttoSocialistmeeting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Benazir_BhuttoSocialistmeeting.jpg/220px-Benazir_BhuttoSocialistmeeting.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Benazir_BhuttoSocialistmeeting.jpg/330px-Benazir_BhuttoSocialistmeeting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Benazir_BhuttoSocialistmeeting.jpg/440px-Benazir_BhuttoSocialistmeeting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benazir_BhuttoSocialistmeeting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Benazir Bhutto interview during <a href="/wiki/Socialist_International" title="Socialist International">Socialist International</a> meeting in 2007.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Assisted by <a href="/wiki/Luis_Ayala" title="Luis Ayala">Luis Ayala</a>, the secretary-general of the Socialist International, in 2006 Bhutto and Nawaz began a process of reconciliation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008108_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008108-246">[245]</a></sup> Ayala believed that this was a prerequisite for ensuring Pakistan's transition back to democratic elections.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008108_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008108-246">[245]</a></sup> Both where then living in London, not far from one another.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008108_246-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008108-246">[245]</a></sup> Facilitated by the lawyer <a href="/wiki/Aitzaz_Ahsan" title="Aitzaz Ahsan">Aitzaz Ahsan</a>, the pair developed a joint plan of action.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008108_246-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008108-246">[245]</a></sup> This entailed establishing a committee consisting of four Pakistani senators, two from the PPP and two from the Pakistan Muslim League (Nawaz).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008108_246-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008108-246">[245]</a></sup> The pair's reconciliation was formalised with the signing of a Charter of Democracy in May 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008109Mu.C3.B1oz2013114_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008109Mu.C3.B1oz2013114-247">[246]</a></sup> Henceforth, Bhutto avoided openly criticising Nawaz as she once had.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008109_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008109-248">[247]</a></sup></p>
<p>Concerned about the instability of their ally, the U.S. government pushed Musharraf to meet with Bhutto and come to an arrangement that might strengthen his legitimacy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008116_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008116-249">[248]</a></sup> This dialogue was also pushed for by the UK government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013118_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013118-250">[249]</a></sup> In January 2007, Musharraf held his first meeting with Bhutto at a hotel in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008112Mu.C3.B1oz2013120_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008112Mu.C3.B1oz2013120-251">[250]</a></sup> The pair underwent follow-up talks in June.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008112_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008112-212">[211]</a></sup> As a result of their discussions, it was agreed that the Pakistani authorities would drop all charges of corruption against both Bhutto and her husband.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008112.E2.80.93113Mu.C3.B1oz2013120.2C_123_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008112.E2.80.93113Mu.C3.B1oz2013120.2C_123-252">[251]</a></sup> It was also agreed that if Musharraf stepped down from his military positions and was elected as a civilian President, then Bhutto would be willing to serve under him as Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008113Mu.C3.B1oz2013120_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008113Mu.C3.B1oz2013120-253">[252]</a></sup> As part of their negotiations, Musharraf also agreed to lift the ban on individuals serving more than two terms as Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013122_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013122-254">[253]</a></sup> Many of Musharraf's close allies had reservations about his concessions to Bhutto.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013121_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013121-255">[254]</a></sup></p>
<p>The US' <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a> and the UK's <a href="/wiki/Jack_Straw" title="Jack Straw">Jack Straw</a> worked together to ensure a transition back to electoral democracy in Pakistan.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013118_250-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013118-250">[249]</a></sup> In August 2007, the U.S. ambassador to the United Nations, <a href="/wiki/Zalmay_Khalizad" class="mw-redirect" title="Zalmay Khalizad">Zalmay Khalizad</a>, has several meetings with Bhutto in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008116_249-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008116-249">[248]</a></sup> In the city, Bhutto also gave a public talk at the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Foreign_Relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Foreign Relations">Council of Foreign Relations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201323_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201323-256">[255]</a></sup> Bhutto and Khalizad also travelled to a luncheon in <a href="/wiki/Aspen,_Colorado" title="Aspen, Colorado">Aspen, Colorado</a> to meet with prominent U.S. political and business leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008116_249-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008116-249">[248]</a></sup> In October 2007, Musharraf was elected President by Pakistan's parliament. In keeping with the agreement made by Bhutto and Musharraf, the PPP representatives abstained rather than voting against Musharraf's nomination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013124.E2.80.93125_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013124.E2.80.93125-257">[256]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Return_to_Pakistan_and_the_assassination_attempt:_October–December_2007"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Pakistan_and_the_assassination_attempt:_October.E2.80.93December_2007">Return to Pakistan and the assassination attempt: October–December 2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benazir_Bhutto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Return to Pakistan and the assassination attempt: October–December 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benazir_Bhutto_house_arrest_VOA_News.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Benazir_Bhutto_house_arrest_VOA_News.jpg/220px-Benazir_Bhutto_house_arrest_VOA_News.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Benazir_Bhutto_house_arrest_VOA_News.jpg/330px-Benazir_Bhutto_house_arrest_VOA_News.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c4/Benazir_Bhutto_house_arrest_VOA_News.jpg 2x" data-file-width="373" data-file-height="250" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benazir_Bhutto_house_arrest_VOA_News.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
While under <a href="/wiki/House_arrest" title="House arrest">house arrest</a>, Benazir Bhutto speaks to supporters outside her house.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bhutto returned to Pakistan in October 2007, arriving in Karachi.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008114Mu.C3.B1oz201328_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008114Mu.C3.B1oz201328-258">[257]</a></sup> Musharraf was annoyed at her arrival, having requested that she only return after the election.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013126_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013126-259">[258]</a></sup> It was widely thought that she had a strong chance of becoming the country's next Prime Minister in the <a href="/wiki/Pakistani_general_election,_2008" title="Pakistani general election, 2008">2008 national elections</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008114_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008114-260">[259]</a></sup> She described the main problem facing her country as the clash between "moderation and extremism",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201325_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201325-261">[260]</a></sup> and was pessimistic about her safety.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201326_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201326-262">[261]</a></sup> Musharraf himself had survived several assassination attempts by Islamist militants,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008117.E2.80.93118Mu.C3.B1oz2013112_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008117.E2.80.93118Mu.C3.B1oz2013112-263">[262]</a></sup> and warned Bhutto that she too would be a target.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201327_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201327-264">[263]</a></sup> She requested that the US or UK take responsibility for her security, but they refused, and her security detail was instead organised by Musharraf.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013128_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013128-265">[264]</a></sup></p>
<p>While her cavalcade was making its way through a crowd in Karachi, <a href="/wiki/2007_Karachi_bombing" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Karachi bombing">two bombs went off</a>, killing 149 and injuring 402. Bhutto herself was physically unharmed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008119Mu.C3.B1oz201328.E2.80.9329_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008119Mu.C3.B1oz201328.E2.80.9329-266">[265]</a></sup> Bhutto alleged that there were four suicide squads that had been dispatched to eliminate her and that there were key officials in the government involved in the plot; she sent a list naming these officials to Musharraf.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008119Mu.C3.B1oz201330_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008119Mu.C3.B1oz201330-267">[266]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-afterbombingNYT_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afterbombingNYT-268">[267]</a></sup> Bhutto requested that Musharraf bring in the British <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Yard" title="Scotland Yard">Scotland Yard</a> or U.S. <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a> to investigate the crime, but he refused.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201330_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201330-269">[268]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lahore,_Pakistan_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Lahore%2C_Pakistan_2008.jpg/220px-Lahore%2C_Pakistan_2008.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Lahore%2C_Pakistan_2008.jpg/330px-Lahore%2C_Pakistan_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Lahore%2C_Pakistan_2008.jpg/440px-Lahore%2C_Pakistan_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lahore,_Pakistan_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Posters of Benazir for sale in <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">Lahore</a> in the run-up to 2008 elections.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Relations between the pair were further strained when Musharraf declared a state of emergency and suspended the constitution in November.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201331.2C_129_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201331.2C_129-270">[269]</a></sup> The PPP and PML-N launched protests at Musharraf's actions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013129_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013129-271">[270]</a></sup> In November, Bhutto was briefly placed under house arrest.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013129_271-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013129-271">[270]</a></sup> She then publicly denounced Musharraf, fearing that any association with him would damage her credibility.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013130_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013130-272">[271]</a></sup> On 16 December, Musharraf lifted the emergency measures and then retired as army chief.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013131_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013131-273">[272]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 November 2007, Bhutto filed her nomination papers for January's Parliamentary elections; two days later, she filed papers in the Larkana constituency for two regular seats. She did so as former Pakistani Prime Minister Nawaz Sharif, following seven years of exile in <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, made his much-contested return to Pakistan and bid for candidacy.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[273]</a></sup> When sworn in again on 30 November 2007, this time as a civilian president after relinquishing his post as military chief, Musharraf announced his plan to lift the Pakistan's state of emergency rule on 16 December. Bhutto welcomed the announcement and launched a manifesto outlining her party's domestic issues. Bhutto told journalists in Islamabad that her party, the PPP, would focus on "the five E's": employment, education, energy, environment, equality.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[275]</a></sup> The PPP's manifesto called for greater civilian oversight of, and restrictions on, the military and intelligence agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013169_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013169-277">[276]</a></sup> They also vowed to rid the intelligence services of elements driven by political or religious motives.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013169_277-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013169-277">[276]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 December 2007, Bhutto met with Nawaz Sharif to publicise their demand that Musharraf fulfill his promise to lift the state of emergency before January's parliamentary elections, threatening to boycott the vote if he failed to comply. They promised to assemble a committee that would present to Musharraf the list of demands upon which their participation in the election was contingent.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[277]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[278]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Assassination">Assassination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benazir_Bhutto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Assassination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Benazir_Bhutto" title="Assassination of Benazir Bhutto">Assassination of Benazir Bhutto</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_reaction_to_the_assassination_of_Benazir_Bhutto" title="International reaction to the assassination of Benazir Bhutto">International reaction to the assassination of Benazir Bhutto</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mausoleum_of_Zulfikar_Ali_Bhutto_and_Benazir_Bhutto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Mausoleum_of_Zulfikar_Ali_Bhutto_and_Benazir_Bhutto.jpg/220px-Mausoleum_of_Zulfikar_Ali_Bhutto_and_Benazir_Bhutto.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Mausoleum_of_Zulfikar_Ali_Bhutto_and_Benazir_Bhutto.jpg/330px-Mausoleum_of_Zulfikar_Ali_Bhutto_and_Benazir_Bhutto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Mausoleum_of_Zulfikar_Ali_Bhutto_and_Benazir_Bhutto.jpg/440px-Mausoleum_of_Zulfikar_Ali_Bhutto_and_Benazir_Bhutto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mausoleum_of_Zulfikar_Ali_Bhutto_and_Benazir_Bhutto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bhutto_family_mausoleum" title="Bhutto family mausoleum">Mausoleum of Bhutto family</a> at the family graveyard <a href="/wiki/Garhi_Khuda_Bakhsh" title="Garhi Khuda Bakhsh">Garhi Khuda Bakhsh</a>, where Benazir Bhutto and several members of her family are buried</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the morning of 27 December, Bhutto met with Afghan President <a href="/wiki/Hamid_Karzai" title="Hamid Karzai">Hamid Karzai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013134.E2.80.93135_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013134.E2.80.93135-280">[279]</a></sup> In the afternoon, she gave a speech at a PPP rally held in <a href="/wiki/Rawalpindi" title="Rawalpindi">Rawalpindi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Liaquat_National_Bagh" class="mw-redirect" title="Liaquat National Bagh">Liaquat National Bagh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201331.2C_137.E2.80.93138_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201331.2C_137.E2.80.93138-281">[280]</a></sup> On leaving in a bulletproof vehicle, she opened the car's escape hatch and stood up to wave to the surrounding crowds.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201332.2C_137.E2.80.93138_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201332.2C_137.E2.80.93138-282">[281]</a></sup> A man stood within two to three metres of the car, fired three gunshots at her, and detonated a suicide vest packed with <a href="/wiki/Ball_bearings" class="mw-redirect" title="Ball bearings">ball bearings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201332.2C_142.E2.80.93143_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201332.2C_142.E2.80.93143-283">[282]</a></sup> Bhutto was fatally injured; reports differ as to whether she was hit by bullets or by shrapnel from the explosion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008120Mu.C3.B1oz201332_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008120Mu.C3.B1oz201332-284">[283]</a></sup> Bhutto was rushed to <a href="/wiki/Rawalpindi_General_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="Rawalpindi General Hospital">Rawalpindi General Hospital</a>, but was <a href="/wiki/Clinically_dead" class="mw-redirect" title="Clinically dead">clinically dead</a> on arrival and attempts at resuscitation were unsuccessful.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201334.2C_144.E2.80.93146_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201334.2C_144.E2.80.93146-285">[284]</a></sup> No autopsy was conducted, and the body was swiftly transported to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chaklala_Air_Base&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chaklala Air Base (page does not exist)">Chaklala Air Base</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013146.E2.80.93147_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013146.E2.80.93147-286">[285]</a></sup> The following day, she was buried next to her father in the <a href="/wiki/Bhutto_family_mausoleum" title="Bhutto family mausoleum">Bhutto family mausoleum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garhi_Khuda_Baksh" class="mw-redirect" title="Garhi Khuda Baksh">Garhi Khuda Baksh</a>, her family graveyard near Larkana.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008121Mu.C3.B1oz2013150_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008121Mu.C3.B1oz2013150-287">[286]</a></sup> PPP supporters rioted in various parts of Pakistan.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013150_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013150-288">[287]</a></sup></p>
<p>Authorities claimed that the assassin had been a teenage boy from <a href="/wiki/South_Waziristan" title="South Waziristan">South Waziristan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013162_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013162-289">[288]</a></sup> They claimed to have proof that the attack had been masterminded by <a href="/wiki/Baitullah_Mehsud" title="Baitullah Mehsud">Baitullah Mehsud</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Pakistani_Taliban" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakistani Taliban">Pakistani Taliban</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008121Mu.C3.B1oz201334_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008121Mu.C3.B1oz201334-290">[289]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[290]</a></sup> The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> concurred that this was probable;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201334_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201334-292">[291]</a></sup> Mehsud believed that Bhutto's pro-American and secularist agenda would undermine the Pakistani Taliban's control of South Waziristan and hinder the growth of Sunni Islamist radicalism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013165_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013165-293">[292]</a></sup> Mehsud denied the accusation,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008121Mu.C3.B1oz2013164_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008121Mu.C3.B1oz2013164-294">[293]</a></sup> with al-Qaeda spokesman <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Abu_al-Yazid" class="mw-redirect" title="Mustafa Abu al-Yazid">Mustafa Abu al-Yazid</a> instead claiming that his organisation had carried out the killing on the order of its second-in-command, <a href="/wiki/Ayman_al-Zawahiri" title="Ayman al-Zawahiri">Ayman al-Zawahiri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013165_293-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013165-293">[292]</a></sup> The PPP accused the government of a cover-up,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013154_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013154-295">[294]</a></sup> with several PPP figures claiming that Bhutto had been killed by a sniper linked to the intelligence agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201335_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201335-296">[295]</a></sup> Within Pakistan there was also public speculation that the attack might have been masterminded by India, or the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008121_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008121-297">[296]</a></sup> Musharraf agreed to invite Britain's <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Yard" title="Scotland Yard">Scotland Yard</a> to investigate the assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201335.2C_161.E2.80.93162_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201335.2C_161.E2.80.93162-298">[297]</a></sup> Requests for the body to be exhumed for an autopsy were rejected by Zardari.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008123Mu.C3.B1oz201334_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008123Mu.C3.B1oz201334-299">[298]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Memorail_of_Benazir_Bhutto.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Memorail_of_Benazir_Bhutto.JPG/220px-Memorail_of_Benazir_Bhutto.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Memorail_of_Benazir_Bhutto.JPG/330px-Memorail_of_Benazir_Bhutto.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Memorail_of_Benazir_Bhutto.JPG/440px-Memorail_of_Benazir_Bhutto.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Memorail_of_Benazir_Bhutto.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Memorial at the site of the assassination</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The election was postponed from January to February 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201378_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201378-300">[299]</a></sup> and was won by a coalition established between the PPP and the <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Muslim_League_(N)" title="Pakistan Muslim League (N)">Pakistan Muslim League (N)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201378_300-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201378-300">[299]</a></sup> The new coalition put forth <a href="/wiki/Yousuf_Raza_Gilani" class="mw-redirect" title="Yousuf Raza Gilani">Yousuf Raza Gilani</a> as Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201378_300-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201378-300">[299]</a></sup> Musharraf, facing likely impeachment, resigned as president In August.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201378_300-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201378-300">[299]</a></sup> He fled to London, although in February 2011 a Rawalpindi court issued a subpoena for him on the grounds that he had not acted on known threats to Bhutto and had provided insufficient security to protect her.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013200_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013200-301">[300]</a></sup> In Bhutto's political will, she had designated her husband <a href="/wiki/Asif_Ali_Zardari" title="Asif Ali Zardari">Asif Ali Zardari</a> as her political successor but Zardari made their nineteen-year-old son, <a href="/wiki/Bilawal_Bhutto_Zardari" title="Bilawal Bhutto Zardari">Bilawal</a>, the Chairman of the PPP <sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[301]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cbsnews_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbsnews-303">[302]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[303]</a></sup> and he became co-chair of the PPP.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201378_300-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201378-300">[299]</a></sup> In September 2008, Zardari was elected President of Pakistan by the country's electoral college.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201335.2C_78.E2.80.9379_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201335.2C_78.E2.80.9379-305">[304]</a></sup></p>
<p>As president, Zardari called for a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> investigation into his wife's assassination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201335_296-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201335-296">[295]</a></sup> In 2009, Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> established a three-person team to lead the investigation comprising the Chilean <a href="/wiki/Heraldo_Mu%C3%B1oz" title="Heraldo Muñoz">Heraldo Muñoz</a>, Irish <a href="/wiki/Peter_FitzGerald" title="Peter FitzGerald">Peter FitzGerald</a>, and Indonesian <a href="/wiki/Marzuki_Darusman" title="Marzuki Darusman">Marzuki Darusman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201315.2C_80.2C_82_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201315.2C_80.2C_82-306">[305]</a></sup> Although it was not in the commission's remit to identify a culprit,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013199_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013199-307">[306]</a></sup> Muñoz later expressed the view that the assassination was likely carried out by the Pakistani Taliban, perhaps with the support of Mehsud, and that they may well have been assisted by rogue elements in the country's intelligence agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013181_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013181-308">[307]</a></sup> He also expressed the view that the original police investigation had been deliberately botched.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013161.E2.80.93162_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013161.E2.80.93162-309">[308]</a></sup> In February 2012, the Pakistani official enquiry issued its final report, placing responsibility for the attack with 27 different militant groups.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013201.E2.80.93202_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013201.E2.80.93202-310">[309]</a></sup> In May 2013, the state's main prosecutor in the Bhutto case, Zulfikar Ali, was himself assassinated in Islamabad.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013200_301-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013200-301">[300]</a></sup> There was never a <a href="/wiki/Smoking_gun" title="Smoking gun">smoking gun</a> in the Bhutto investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013181_308-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013181-308">[307]</a></sup> Many in Pakistan had reasons for wanting Bhutto dead;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013181_308-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013181-308">[307]</a></sup> her killing was advantageous to both the military establishment and to the Islamic fundamentalists who despised her.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008124_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008124-311">[310]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideology">Ideology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benazir_Bhutto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Ideology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bhatia described Bhutto as having "liberal convictions" and a "self-evidently progressive outlook".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008x.2C_xi_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008x.2C_xi-312">[311]</a></sup> Bhutto regarded herself as an ardent supporter of women's rights,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia20082_313-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia20082-313">[312]</a></sup> and took a hard stance against militant Islamism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013168_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013168-314">[313]</a></sup> Although she had to compromise with Pakistan's powerful Islamist lobby, she favoured a secular government for the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELamb199131_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELamb199131-315">[314]</a></sup> Under Bhutto's leadership, the PPP was officially secular,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013168_314-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013168-314">[313]</a></sup> as were the governments which she led.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELamb199130_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELamb199130-87">[87]</a></sup> She admired the <a href="/wiki/Thatcherism" title="Thatcherism">Thatcherite</a> economic policies pursued by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a> in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELamb199130_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELamb199130-87">[87]</a></sup> She advocated for the creation of an expanded economically and politically stable middle-class in Pakistan, believing that this was needed in order to sustain a stable democratic state.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013228_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013228-316">[315]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bhutto described her main role model as <a href="/wiki/Fatimah" title="Fatimah">Fatimah</a>, the daughter of the Islamic prophet <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>, stating that she admired her piety, wisdom, and courage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20085_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20085-317">[316]</a></sup> She also described the Indian Prime Minister Indira Gandhi as a political inspiration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20085_317-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20085-317">[316]</a></sup> Lamb described Bhutto at being skilled in using <a href="/wiki/Populism" title="Populism">populist</a> strategies in election campaigns.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELamb199194_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELamb199194-318">[317]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benazir_Bhutto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personality">Personality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benazir_Bhutto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Personality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25em; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>Familial charisma is rare, but in Benazir's case the Bhutto name matters, in that her father's charisma easily transferred to her. She had her own charisma when she emerged in the 1980s as a young, articulate, well-educated and well-spoken woman. Her chief assets were her intelligence, her confidence, and the fact that she could talk to people of various backgrounds with empathy. She had the rare quality of humour, which she never lost in spite of leading an uncertain and challenging life. Above all, she could use the media effectively. Her faults as a political leader were many. Too many stories of corruption stuck to her. She was not a good administrator. She was too inclined to listen to her small kitchen cabinet, which very often consisted of people who would say what they thought she wanted to hear. She became prime minister at a particularly young age and had no prior political or other cabinet experience.</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">— Islamic studies scholar Akbar S. Ahmed, 2008<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed2008_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed2008-319">[318]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>According to Bhutto biographer Shyam Bhatia, Bhutto had a desire to be liked and to be popular, and for this reason "was prepared to be all things to all people", having a "chameleon-like" quality to blend into her environment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia20085_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia20085-320">[319]</a></sup> He for instance noted that while in Pakistan she presented herself as a conservative Muslim who always wore her head covered, while as a student in Oxford she adopted a more liberal lifestyle, tending to wear a T-shirt and jeans and occasionally drinking wine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia20082_313-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia20082-313">[312]</a></sup> Muñoz concurred, describing Bhutto as "a woman of contradictions".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201319_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201319-14">[14]</a></sup> As a politician, she was conscious of how her image was presented in Pakistan; she dressed modestly, was never photographed with a glass lest it be interpreted as containing alcohol, and would refuse to shake men's hands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20084_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20084-321">[320]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Islamic studies scholar <a href="/wiki/Akbar_S._Ahmed" class="mw-redirect" title="Akbar S. Ahmed">Akbar S. Ahmed</a>, who went to school with Bhutto, noted that she was a "pampered and precocious" child.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20084_321-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20084-321">[320]</a></sup> Bhatia claimed that at Oxford, where he first met her, Bhutto was spoilt, self-obsessed, and prone to throwing temper tantrums, although at the same time was humourous and generous, willing to pay for her friends' meals whenever at a restaurant.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia20083_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia20083-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Having encountered her later in life, Muñoz regarded Bhutto as a "charming and intelligent" woman.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201318_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201318-322">[321]</a></sup> Ahmed stated that "her father's charisma easily transferred to her."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20084_321-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20084-321">[320]</a></sup> The journalist <a href="/wiki/Christina_Lamb" title="Christina Lamb">Christina Lamb</a> noted that Bhutto shared her father's charisma and arrogance,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELamb199114_323-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELamb199114-323">[322]</a></sup> and was also impatient of criticism in a manner similar to him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELamb199116_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELamb199116-324">[323]</a></sup> Lamb also believed that in being raised in a wealthy and aristocratic family, Bhutto was unable to appreciate the struggles of Pakistan's poorest.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELamb199129_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELamb199129-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Close friends called her "BB" or "Pinkie", the latter being the childhood nickname given her by her parents.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia20081_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia20081-89">[89]</a></sup> Bhutto was devoted to her father and husband.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008126_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008126-325">[324]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[325]</a></sup> In later life, she increasingly came to see success through the prism of her family.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008125_327-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia2008125-327">[326]</a></sup> She had a love of French and Italian cuisine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia20085_320-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia20085-320">[319]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benazir_Bhutto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benazir_Bhutto_US_visit_19890605.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Benazir_Bhutto_US_visit_19890605.jpg/220px-Benazir_Bhutto_US_visit_19890605.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Benazir_Bhutto_US_visit_19890605.jpg/330px-Benazir_Bhutto_US_visit_19890605.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Benazir_Bhutto_US_visit_19890605.jpg/440px-Benazir_Bhutto_US_visit_19890605.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2830" data-file-height="1900" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benazir_Bhutto_US_visit_19890605.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Benazir Bhutto, carrying her son Bilawal Bhutto Zardari, leaving an airliner upon her arrival for a state visit with husband <a href="/wiki/Asif_Ali_Zardari" title="Asif Ali Zardari">Asif Ali Zardari</a> (in background)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Zardari_family" title="Zardari family">Zardari family</a></div>
<p>On returning to Pakistan in the 1980s, Bhutto's mother organised for her to marry the businessman <a href="/wiki/Asif_Ali_Zardari" title="Asif Ali Zardari">Asif Ali Zardari</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia20084_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia20084-31">[31]</a></sup> Many of her friends were surprised that Bhutto acquiesced to an arranged marriage given her liberal attitudes, however she later related that she "felt obligations to my family and my religion" to go through with it and that her high public profile made it difficult for her to find a husband through other means.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia200828_328-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia200828-328">[327]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 December 1987, Bhutto married Asif Ali Zardari in an arranged marriage at Karachi. The couple had three children: a son, <a href="/wiki/Bilawal_Bhutto_Zardari" title="Bilawal Bhutto Zardari">Bilawal</a> and two daughters, <a href="/wiki/Bakhtawar_Bhutto_Zardari" title="Bakhtawar Bhutto Zardari">Bakhtawar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aseefa_Bhutto_Zardari" title="Aseefa Bhutto Zardari">Aseefa</a>. When she gave birth to Bakhtawar in 1990, she became the first modern head of government to give birth while in office.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[328]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benazir_Bhutto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Benazir_Bhutto_University_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Benazir Bhutto University (disambiguation)">List of things named after Benazir Bhutto</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benazir_bhutto_1988_(square).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Benazir_bhutto_1988_%28square%29.jpg/200px-Benazir_bhutto_1988_%28square%29.jpg" width="200" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Benazir_bhutto_1988_%28square%29.jpg/300px-Benazir_bhutto_1988_%28square%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Benazir_bhutto_1988_%28square%29.jpg/400px-Benazir_bhutto_1988_%28square%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="513" data-file-height="513" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benazir_bhutto_1988_(square).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bhutto left a deeply polarizing legacy</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benazir_Bhutto_memorial_coin_obverse.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Benazir_Bhutto_memorial_coin_obverse.JPG/200px-Benazir_Bhutto_memorial_coin_obverse.JPG" width="200" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Benazir_Bhutto_memorial_coin_obverse.JPG/300px-Benazir_Bhutto_memorial_coin_obverse.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Benazir_Bhutto_memorial_coin_obverse.JPG/400px-Benazir_Bhutto_memorial_coin_obverse.JPG 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benazir_Bhutto_memorial_coin_obverse.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Benazir Bhutto memorial coin, commemorative coin of Pakistan.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Muñoz described her as "one of Pakistan's most important political figures, a respected world leader, and the leading stateswoman in the Islamic world".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201319_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201319-14">[14]</a></sup> Ahmed stated that she was one of very few political leaders who had been able to "assume the iconic status of a political martyr in the West while simultaneously evoking strong sentiments in the Muslim world."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed2008_319-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed2008-319">[318]</a></sup> He therefore contrasted her with contemporaries like Iraq's <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein" title="Saddam Hussein">Saddam Hussein</a> who were popular domestically but hated in the West, and those like Egypt's <a href="/wiki/Hosni_Mubarak" title="Hosni Mubarak">Hosni Mubarak</a> who curried favour with Western governments while alienating their domestic audience.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed2008_319-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed2008-319">[318]</a></sup> Comparisons were often made between Bhutto and the Filipino exile-come-political leader <a href="/wiki/Corazon_Aquino" title="Corazon Aquino">Corazon Aquino</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELamb199146_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELamb199146-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Within the Islamic world, Bhutto was often regarded as "a genuine Muslim political leader" and recognised as the leader of Pakistan's most popular political party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20084_321-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20084-321">[320]</a></sup> At the same time there were many Pakistanis who despised her, disliking her popularity, her ties to Western nations, and her modernising agenda.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201319_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201319-14">[14]</a></sup> Extremist Sunni Islamist elements opposed her leadership because they believed it wrong for a woman to lead an Islamic society, and because they believed that she was in reality a Shia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013168_314-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013168-314">[313]</a></sup> She gained popularity in Western nations in part because she could present herself as being "part of their world", speaking a high standard of English and having been educated at Harvard and Oxford.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20084_321-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoutmanAhmed20084-321">[320]</a></sup> In the West, her supporters sometimes had doubts about her ability to govern, but they generally viewed her as a progressive figure who could advance democracy and counter-terrorism in Pakistan.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201319_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz201319-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Commenting on her legacy, William Dalrymple writes that "it's wrong for the West simply to mourn Benazir Bhutto as a martyred democrat since her legacy was far murkier and more complex".<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-224">[223]</a></sup> Despite her western and positive image in the world, Bhutto's controversial policies and support have made her legacy much more complicated.<sup id="cite_ref-MixedLegacy_330-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MixedLegacy-330">[329]</a></sup> Benazir Bhutto failed to revert the controversial Hudood Ordinance — a controversial presidential ordinance which suppressed women's rights, making them subordinate to men.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_224-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-224">[223]</a></sup> In 2009, the <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a>, described her legacy as "mixed", and commented that: "it's only in death that she will become an icon—in some ways people will look at her accomplishments through rose-tinted glasses rather than remembering the corruption charges, her lack of achievements or how much she was manipulated by other people."<sup id="cite_ref-MixedLegacy_330-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MixedLegacy-330">[329]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, writing about Benazir, termed her "[both] a victim, as well as in part a culprit, of its [Pakistan's] chronic instability".<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[330]</a></sup> Writing her <a href="/wiki/Obituary" title="Obituary">obituary</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> referred her as "a woman of grand aspirations with a taste for complex political maneuverings".<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[331]</a></sup> Journalist <i>Adele M. Stan</i> published an article on <i><a href="/wiki/The_American_Prospect" title="The American Prospect">The American Prospect</a></i> after her death calling Bhutto "An Imperfect Feminist" and noted "Though she looked like a walking holy card, Bhutto was hardly a saint. Said to have presided over something of a <a href="/wiki/Kleptocracy" title="Kleptocracy">kleptocracy</a> during her two terms as prime minister, Bhutto also, for all her railing against the mullahs, cut her deals with the religious parties and supported the Taliban's rise to power in neighboring Afghanistan." <sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[332]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bhutto became a global icon for women's rights.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBhatia20084_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhatia20084-31">[31]</a></sup> Bhutto was the first woman in the world to head a <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">Muslim majority country</a>, which influenced other Muslim women to follow her path.Her fight-for-right policy has influenced a number of people, including the youngest-ever <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> laureate <a href="/wiki/Malala_Yousafzai" title="Malala Yousafzai">Malala Yousafzai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reporter_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reporter-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tribune.com.pk_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tribune.com.pk-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Her efforts and struggle to save her father and democracy remain a lasting legacy that is deeply respected among her rivals. Several <a href="/wiki/Benazir_Bhutto_University_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Benazir Bhutto University (disambiguation)">universities and public buildings</a> in Pakistan have been named after her. The Pakistani government honored Bhutto on her birthday by renaming Islamabad's airport <a href="/wiki/Benazir_Bhutto_International_Airport" title="Benazir Bhutto International Airport">Benazir Bhutto International Airport</a>, Muree Road of Rawalpindi as Benazir Bhutto Road<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and Rawalpindi General Hospital as Benazir Bhutto Hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013145_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMu.C3.B1oz2013145-334">[333]</a></sup> Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Yousaf_Raza_Gillani" title="Yousaf Raza Gillani">Yousaf Raza Gillani</a>, a member of Bhutto's PPP, also asked President Pervez Musharraf to pardon convicts on death row on her birthday in honour of Bhutto.<sup id="cite_ref-RX_335-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RX-335">[334]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Authored_books">Authored books</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Benazir_Bhutto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Authored books">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>

<li><cite class="citation book"><i><a href="/wiki/Reconciliation:_Islam,_Democracy,_and_the_West" title="Reconciliation: Islam, Democracy, and the West">Reconciliation: Islam, Democracy, and the West</a></i>. HarperCollins. 2008. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-06-156758-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-06-156758-2">978-0-06-156758-2</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABenazir+Bhutto&amp;rft.btitle=Reconciliation%3A+Islam%2C+Democracy%2C+and+the+West&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-06-156758-2&amp;rft.pub=HarperCollins&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
</ul>

<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">

<li id="cite_note-tribune.com.pk-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-tribune.com.pk_2-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-tribune.com.pk_2-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://tribune.com.pk/story/804589/malala-yousafzai-17-to-receive-nobel-peace-prize/">"Following in Benazir's footsteps, Malala aspires to become PM of Pakistan – The Express Tribune"</a>. 2014-12-10<span class="reference-accessdate">.
